Senate File 226 - Introduced


                                 SENATE FILE 

                                 SENATE FILE 
                                 SENATE FILE                                  SENATE FILE                                  BY  TAYLOR

 A BILL FOR

  1 An Act relating to creation of transfer on death deeds and to
  2    disclaimers of an interest in real property, and including
  3    applicability provisions.
  4 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:
    TLSB 2171XS (4) 87
    jh/rj

  1  4    Sec. 2.    1  4    Sec. 2.    1  5    As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise
  1  6 requires:
  1  7    1.  "Beneficiary" means a person that receives property under
  1  8 a transfer on death deed.
  1  9    2.  "Designated beneficiary" means a person designated to
  1 10 receive property in a transfer on death deed.
  1 11    3.  "Joint owner" means an individual who owns property
  1 12 concurrently with one or more other individuals with a right of
  1 13 survivorship. "Joint owner" includes a joint tenant and tenant
  1 14 by the entirety. "Joint owner" does not include a tenant in
  1 15 common.
  1 16    4.  "Person" means an individual, corporation, business
  1 17 trust, estate, trust, partnership, limited liability company,
  1 18 association, joint venture, public corporation, government or
  1 19 governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality, or any
  1 20 other legal or commercial entity.
  1 21    5.  "Property" means an interest in real property located in
  1 22 this state which is transferable on the death of the owner.
  1 23    6.  "Transfer on death deed" means a deed authorized under
  1 24 this chapter.
  1 25    7.  "Transferor" means an individual who makes a transfer on
  1 26 death deed.

  2 14    Sec. 9.    2 14    Sec. 9.    2 15    A transfer on death deed:
  2 16    1.  Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, must
  2 17 contain the essential elements and formalities of a properly
  2 18 recordable inter vivos deed.
  2 19    2.  Must state that the transfer to the designated
  2 20 beneficiary is to occur at the transferor's death.
  2 21    3.  Must be recorded before the transferor's death in the
  2 22 public records in the office of the county recorder in the
  2 23 county where the property is located.

  2 31    Sec. 11.    2 31    Sec. 11.    2 32 authorized ==== revocation by act not permitted.
  2 33    1.  Subject to subsection 2, an instrument is effective to
  2 34 revoke a recorded transfer on death deed, or any part of the
  2 35 deed, only if all of the following apply:
  3  1    a.  The instrument is any of the following:
  3  2    (1)  A transfer on death deed that revokes the deed or part
  3  3 of the deed expressly or by inconsistency.
  3  4    (2)  An instrument of revocation that expressly revokes the
  3  5 deed or part of the deed.
  3  6    (3)  An inter vivos deed that expressly revokes the transfer
  3  7 on death deed or part of the deed.
  3  8    b.  The instrument is acknowledged by the transferor after
  3  9 the acknowledgment of the deed being revoked and is recorded
  3 10 before the transferor's death in the public records in the
  3 11 office of the county recorder of the county where the deed is
  3 12 recorded.
  3 13    2.  If a transfer on death deed is made by more than one
  3 14 transferor, all of the following apply:
  3 15    a.  Revocation by a transferor does not affect the deed as to
  3 16 the interest of another transferor.
  3 17    b.  A deed of joint owners is revoked only if the deed is
  3 18 revoked by all of the living joint owners.
  3 19    3.  After a transfer on death deed is recorded, the deed
  3 20 cannot be revoked by a revocatory act on the deed.
  3 21    4.  This section does not limit the effect of an inter vivos
  3 22 transfer of the property.
  3 23    Sec. 12.    2 33    1.  Subject to subsection 2, an instrument is effective to

  3  3 of the deed expressly or by inconsistency.

  3  5 deed or part of the deed.
  3  6    (3)  An inter vivos deed that expressly revokes the transfer
  3  7 on death deed or part of the deed.
  3  8    b.  The instrument is acknowledged by the transferor after
  3  9 the acknowledgment of the deed being revoked and is recorded
  3 10 before the transferor's death in the public records in the
  3 11 office of the county recorder of the county where the deed is
  3 12 recorded.
  3 13    2.  If a transfer on death deed is made by more than one
  3 14 transferor, all of the following apply:
  3 15    a.  Revocation by a transferor does not affect the deed as to
  3 16 the interest of another transferor.
  3 17    b.  A deed of joint owners is revoked only if the deed is
  3 18 revoked by all of the living joint owners.
  3 19    3.  After a transfer on death deed is recorded, the deed
  3 20 cannot be revoked by a revocatory act on the deed.
  3 21    4.  This section does not limit the effect of an inter vivos
  3 22 transfer of the property.

  3 23    Sec. 12.    3 23    Sec. 12.    3 24 deed during transferor's life.
  3 25    During a transferor's life, a transfer on death deed does not
  3 26 do any of the following:
  3 27    1.  Affect an interest or right of the transferor or any
  3 28 other owner, including the right to transfer or encumber the
  3 29 property.
  3 30    2.  Affect an interest or right of a transferee, even if the
  3 31 transferee has actual or constructive notice of the deed.
  3 32    3.  Affect an interest or right of a secured or unsecured
  3 33 creditor or future creditor of the transferor, even if the
  3 34 creditor has actual or constructive notice of the deed.
  3 35    4.  Affect the transferor's or designated beneficiary's
  4  1 eligibility for any form of public assistance.
  4  2    5.  Create a legal or equitable interest in favor of the
  4  3 designated beneficiary.
  4  4    6.  Subject the property to claims or process of a creditor
  4  5 of the designated beneficiary.
  4  6    Sec. 13.    3 25    During a transferor's life, a transfer on death deed does not
  3 26 do any of the following:
  3 27    1.  Affect an interest or right of the transferor or any
  3 28 other owner, including the right to transfer or encumber the
  3 29 property.

  4  6    Sec. 13.    4  6    Sec. 13.    4  7 deed at transferor's death.
  4  8    1.  Except as otherwise provided in the transfer on death
  4  9 deed, in this section, or in section 633.238, 633.523, or
  4 10 633.535, upon the death of the transferor, the following rules
  4 11 apply to property that is the subject of a transfer on death
  4 12 deed and owned by the transferor at death:
  4 13    a.  Subject to paragraph "b", the interest in the property is
  4 14 transferred to the designated beneficiary in accordance with
  4 15 the deed.
  4 16    b.  The interest of a designated beneficiary is contingent
  4 17 on the designated beneficiary surviving the transferor. The
  4 18 interest of a designated beneficiary that fails to survive the
  4 19 transferor lapses.
  4 20    c.  Subject to paragraph "d", concurrent interests are
  4 21 transferred to the beneficiaries in equal and undivided shares
  4 22 with no right of survivorship.
  4 23    d.  If the transferor has identified two or more designated
  4 24 beneficiaries to receive concurrent interests in the property,
  4 25 the share of one which lapses or fails for any reason is
  4 26 transferred to the other, or to the others in proportion to the
  4 27 interest of each in the remaining part of the property held
  4 28 concurrently.
  4 29    2.  Subject to section 558.41, a beneficiary takes the
  4 30 property subject to all conveyances, encumbrances, assignments,
  4 31 contracts, mortgages, liens, and other interests to which the
  4 32 property is subject at the transferor's death. For purposes
  4 33 of this subsection and section 558.41, the recording of the
  4 34 transfer on death deed is deemed to have occurred at the
  4 35 transferor's death.
  5  1    3.  a.  If a transferor is a joint owner and is survived
  5  2 by one or more other joint owners, the property that is the
  5  3 subject of a transfer on death deed belongs to the surviving
  5  4 joint owner or owners with right of survivorship.
  5  5    b.  If a transferor is the last surviving joint owner, the
  5  6 transfer on death deed is effective.
  5  7    4.  A transfer on death deed transfers property without
  5  8 covenant or warranty of title even if the deed contains a
  5  9 contrary provision.
  5 10    Sec. 14.    4  8    1.  Except as otherwise provided in the transfer on death
  4  9 deed, in this section, or in section 633.238, 633.523, or
  4 10 633.535, upon the death of the transferor, the following rules
  4 11 apply to property that is the subject of a transfer on death
  4 12 deed and owned by the transferor at death:
  4 13    a.  Subject to paragraph "b", the interest in the property is
  4 14 transferred to the designated beneficiary in accordance with
  4 15 the deed.
  4 16    b.  The interest of a designated beneficiary is contingent
  4 17 on the designated beneficiary surviving the transferor. The
  4 18 interest of a designated beneficiary that fails to survive the
  4 19 transferor lapses.
  4 20    c.  Subject to paragraph "d", concurrent interests are
  4 21 transferred to the beneficiaries in equal and undivided shares
  4 22 with no right of survivorship.
  4 23    d.  If the transferor has identified two or more designated
  4 24 beneficiaries to receive concurrent interests in the property,
  4 25 the share of one which lapses or fails for any reason is
  4 26 transferred to the other, or to the others in proportion to the
  4 27 interest of each in the remaining part of the property held
  4 28 concurrently.
  4 29    2.  Subject to section 558.41, a beneficiary takes the
  4 30 property subject to all conveyances, encumbrances, assignments,
  4 31 contracts, mortgages, liens, and other interests to which the
  4 32 property is subject at the transferor's death. For purposes
  4 33 of this subsection and section 558.41, the recording of the
  4 34 transfer on death deed is deemed to have occurred at the
  4 35 transferor's death.
  5  1    3.  a.  If a transferor is a joint owner and is survived
  5  2 by one or more other joint owners, the property that is the
  5  3 subject of a transfer on death deed belongs to the surviving
  5  4 joint owner or owners with right of survivorship.
  5  5    b.  If a transferor is the last surviving joint owner, the
  5  6 transfer on death deed is effective.
  5  7    4.  A transfer on death deed transfers property without
  5  8 covenant or warranty of title even if the deed contains a
  5  9 contrary provision.

  5 13    Sec. 15.    5 13    Sec. 15.    5 14 and statutory allowances.
  5 15    1.  To the extent the transferor's probate estate is
  5 16 insufficient to satisfy an allowed claim against the estate
  5 17 or a statutory allowance to a surviving spouse or child, the
  5 18 estate may enforce the liability against property transferred
  5 19 at the transferor's death by a transfer on death deed.
  5 20    2.  If more than one property is transferred by one or more
  5 21 transfer on death deeds, the liability under subsection 1 is
  5 22 apportioned among the properties in proportion to the net
  5 23 values of the properties at the transferor's death.
  5 24    3.  A proceeding to enforce the liability under this section
  5 25 must be commenced not later than eighteen months after the
  5 26 transferor's death.

  5 29    The following form may be used to create a transfer on death
  5 30 deed. The other sections of this chapter govern the effect of
  5 31 this or any other instrument used to create a transfer on death
  5 32 deed:
  5 33    (front of form)
  5 34    REVOCABLE TRANSFER ON DEATH DEED
  5 35    NOTICE TO OWNER
  6  1 You should carefully read all information on the other side
  6  2 of this form. You may want to consult a lawyer before using
  6  3 this form.
  6  4    This form must be recorded before your death, or it will not
  6  5 be effective.
  6  6    IDENTIFYING INFORMATION
  6  7    Owner or owners making this deed
  6  8    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6  9    Printed name                 Mailing address

  6 11    Printed name                 Mailing address
  6 12    Legal description of the property
  6 13    __________________________________________________________
  6 14    PRIMARY BENEFICIARY
  6 15    I designate the following beneficiary if the beneficiary
  6 16 survives me.
  6 17    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 18    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 19    ALTERNATE BENEFICIARY = Optional
  6 20    If my primary beneficiary does not survive me, I designate
  6 21 the following alternate beneficiary if that beneficiary
  6 22 survives me.
  6 23    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 24    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 25    TRANSFER ON DEATH
  6 26    At my death, I transfer my interest in the described property
  6 27 to the beneficiaries as designated above.
  6 28    Before my death, I have the right to revoke this deed.

  7  1 ACKNOWLEDGMENT
  7  2    (insert acknowledgment for deed here)
  7  3    (back of form)
  7  4    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  7  5    What does the Transfer on Death (TOD) deed do?
  7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    5 29    The following form may be used to create a transfer on death
  5 30 deed. The other sections of this chapter govern the effect of
  5 31 this or any other instrument used to create a transfer on death
  5 32 deed:

  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    5 30 deed. The other sections of this chapter govern the effect of
  5 31 this or any other instrument used to create a transfer on death
  5 32 deed:
  5 33    (front of form)
  5 34    REVOCABLE TRANSFER ON DEATH DEED
  5 35    NOTICE TO OWNER
  6  1 You should carefully read all information on the other side
  6  2 of this form. You may want to consult a lawyer before using
  6  3 this form.
  6  4    This form must be recorded before your death, or it will not
  6  5 be effective.
  6  6    IDENTIFYING INFORMATION
  6  7    Owner or owners making this deed
  6  8    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6  9    Printed name                 Mailing address
  6 10    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 11    Printed name                 Mailing address
  6 12    Legal description of the property
  6 13    __________________________________________________________
  6 14    PRIMARY BENEFICIARY
  6 15    I designate the following beneficiary if the beneficiary
  6 16 survives me.
  6 17    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 18    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 19    ALTERNATE BENEFICIARY = Optional
  6 20    If my primary beneficiary does not survive me, I designate
  6 21 the following alternate beneficiary if that beneficiary
  6 22 survives me.
  6 23    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 24    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 25    TRANSFER ON DEATH
  6 26    At my death, I transfer my interest in the described property
  6 27 to the beneficiaries as designated above.
  6 28    Before my death, I have the right to revoke this deed.
  6 29    SIGNATURE OF OWNER OR OWNERS MAKING THIS DEED
  6 30                      Seal, if any
  6 31    Signature                 Date
  6 32    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 33                      Seal, if any
  6 34    Signature                 Date
  6 35    _____________________________                 _________________________
  7  1 ACKNOWLEDGMENT
  7  2    (insert acknowledgment for deed here)
  7  3    (back of form)
  7  4    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  7  5    What does the Transfer on Death (TOD) deed do?
  7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.

  7  5    What does the Transfer on Death (TOD) deed do?
  7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    6  1 You should carefully read all information on the other side
  6  2 of this form. You may want to consult a lawyer before using
  6  3 this form.
  6  4    This form must be recorded before your death, or it will not
  6  5 be effective.

  6  7    Owner or owners making this deed

  6 12    Legal description of the property

  6 16 survives me.
  6 17    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 18    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available

  6 20    If my primary beneficiary does not survive me, I designate
  6 21 the following alternate beneficiary if that beneficiary
  6 22 survives me.
  6 23    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 24    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 25    TRANSFER ON DEATH
  6 26    At my death, I transfer my interest in the described property
  6 27 to the beneficiaries as designated above.
  6 28    Before my death, I have the right to revoke this deed.

  6 13    __________________________________________________________
  6 14    PRIMARY BENEFICIARY
  6 15    I designate the following beneficiary if the beneficiary
  6 16 survives me.
  6 17    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 18    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 19    ALTERNATE BENEFICIARY = Optional
  6 20    If my primary beneficiary does not survive me, I designate
  6 21 the following alternate beneficiary if that beneficiary
  6 22 survives me.
  6 23    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 24    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 25    TRANSFER ON DEATH
  6 26    At my death, I transfer my interest in the described property
  6 27 to the beneficiaries as designated above.
  6 28    Before my death, I have the right to revoke this deed.
  6 29    SIGNATURE OF OWNER OR OWNERS MAKING THIS DEED
  6 30                      Seal, if any
  6 31    Signature                 Date
  6 32    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 33                      Seal, if any
  6 34    Signature                 Date
  6 35    _____________________________                 _________________________
  7  1 ACKNOWLEDGMENT
  7  2    (insert acknowledgment for deed here)
  7  3    (back of form)
  7  4    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  7  5    What does the Transfer on Death (TOD) deed do?
  7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    6  7    Owner or owners making this deed

  6 20    If my primary beneficiary does not survive me, I designate
  6 21 the following alternate beneficiary if that beneficiary
  6 22 survives me.
  6 23    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 24    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 25    TRANSFER ON DEATH
  6 26    At my death, I transfer my interest in the described property
  6 27 to the beneficiaries as designated above.
  6 28    Before my death, I have the right to revoke this deed.
  6 29    SIGNATURE OF OWNER OR OWNERS MAKING THIS DEED
  6 30                      Seal, if any
  6 31    Signature                 Date
  6 32    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 33                      Seal, if any
  6 34    Signature                 Date
  6 35    _____________________________                 _________________________
  7  1 ACKNOWLEDGMENT
  7  2    (insert acknowledgment for deed here)
  7  3    (back of form)
  7  4    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  7  5    What does the Transfer on Death (TOD) deed do?
  7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    6 13    __________________________________________________________

  6 21 the following alternate beneficiary if that beneficiary
  6 22 survives me.

  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    6 19    ALTERNATE BENEFICIARY = Optional
  6 20    If my primary beneficiary does not survive me, I designate
  6 21 the following alternate beneficiary if that beneficiary
  6 22 survives me.
  6 23    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 24    Printed name                 Mailing address, if available
  6 25    TRANSFER ON DEATH
  6 26    At my death, I transfer my interest in the described property
  6 27 to the beneficiaries as designated above.
  6 28    Before my death, I have the right to revoke this deed.
  6 29    SIGNATURE OF OWNER OR OWNERS MAKING THIS DEED
  6 30                      Seal, if any
  6 31    Signature                 Date
  6 32    _____________________________                 _________________________
  6 33                      Seal, if any
  6 34    Signature                 Date
  6 35    _____________________________                 _________________________
  7  1 ACKNOWLEDGMENT
  7  2    (insert acknowledgment for deed here)
  7  3    (back of form)
  7  4    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  7  5    What does the Transfer on Death (TOD) deed do?
  7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.

  8 21 fraud.

  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.

  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    6 26    At my death, I transfer my interest in the described property
  6 27 to the beneficiaries as designated above.
  6 28    Before my death, I have the right to revoke this deed.
  6 29    SIGNATURE OF OWNER OR OWNERS MAKING THIS DEED

  7  4    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  7  5    What does the Transfer on Death (TOD) deed do?
  7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part

  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.

  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.

  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    6 33                      Seal, if any
  6 34    Signature                 Date
  6 35    _____________________________                 _________________________
  7  1 ACKNOWLEDGMENT
  7  2    (insert acknowledgment for deed here)
  7  3    (back of form)
  7  4    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  7  5    What does the Transfer on Death (TOD) deed do?
  7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.

  8 26    Sec. 17.    7  6    When you die, this deed transfers the described property,
  7  7 subject to any liens or mortgages (or other encumbrances) on
  7  8 the property at your death. Probate is not required. The TOD
  7  9 deed has no effect until you die. You can revoke it at any
  7 10 time. You are also free to transfer the property to someone
  7 11 else during your lifetime. If you do not own any interest in
  7 12 the property when you die, this deed will have no effect.
  7 13    How do I make a TOD deed?
  7 14    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a
  7 15 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take
  7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.

  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    7 16 acknowledgments. Record the form in each county where any part
  7 17 of the property is located. The form has no effect unless it is
  7 18 acknowledged and recorded before your death.
  7 19    Is the legal description of the property necessary?
  7 20    Yes.
  7 21    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  7 22    This information may be on the deed you received when you
  7 23 became an owner of the property. This information may also be
  7 24 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  7 25 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
  7 26 consult a lawyer.
  7 27    Can I change my mind before I record the TOD deed?
  7 28    Yes. If you have not yet recorded the deed and want to
  7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.
  8  2    Can I later revoke the TOD deed if I change my mind?
  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.

  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.

  8  3    Yes. You can revoke the TOD deed. No one, including the
  8  4 beneficiaries, can prevent you from revoking the deed.
  8  5    How do I revoke the TOD deed after it is recorded?
  8  6    There are three ways to revoke a recorded TOD deed: [1]
  8  7 Complete and acknowledge a revocation form, and record it in
  8  8 each county where the property is located. [2] Complete and
  8  9 acknowledge a new TOD deed that disposes of the same property,
  8 10 and record it in each county where the property is located.
  8 11 [3] Transfer the property to someone else during your lifetime
  8 12 by a recorded deed that expressly revokes the TOD deed. You
  8 13 may not revoke the TOD deed by will.
  8 14    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
  8 15 do?
  8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
  8 18    Do I need to tell the beneficiaries about the TOD deed?
  8 19    No, but it is recommended.  Secrecy can cause later
  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    7 29 change your mind, simply tear up or otherwise destroy the deed.
  7 30    How do I record the TOD deed?
  7 31    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
  7 32 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
  7 33 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
  7 34 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
  7 35 property is in more than one county, you should record the deed
  8  1 in each county.

  8 20 complications and might make it easier for others to commit
  8 21 fraud.
  8 22    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
  8 23    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
  8 24 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
  8 25 lawyer.
  8 26    Sec. 17.    8 16    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
  8 17 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.

  8 26    Sec. 17.    8 26    Sec. 17.    8 27    The following form may be used to create an instrument of
  8 28 revocation under this chapter.  The other sections of this
  8 29 chapter govern the effect of this or any other instrument used
  8 30 to revoke a transfer on death deed.
  8 31    (front of form)
  8 32    REVOCATION OF TRANSFER ON DEATH DEED
  8 33    NOTICE TO OWNER
  8 34    This revocation must be recorded before you die or it will
  8 35 not be effective. This revocation is effective only as to the
  9  1 interests in the property of owners who sign this revocation.
  9  2    IDENTIFYING INFORMATION
  9  3    Owner or owners of property making this revocation
  9  4    _____________________________                 _________________________
  9  5    Printed name                 Mailing address
  9  6    _____________________________                 _________________________
  9  7    Printed name                 Mailing address
  9  8    Legal description of the property
  9  9 __________________________________________________________
  9 10    REVOCATION
  9 11    I revoke all my previous transfers of this property by
  9 12 transfer on death deed.
  9 13    SIGNATURE OF OWNER OR OWNERS MAKING THIS REVOCATION
  9 14                      Seal, if any
  9 15    Signature                 Date
  9 16    _____________________________                 _________________________
  9 17                      Seal, if any
  9 18    Signature                 Date
  9 19    _____________________________                 _________________________
  9 20    ACKNOWLEDGMENT
  9 21    (insert acknowledgment here)
  9 22    (back of form)
  9 23    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  9 24    How do I use this form to revoke a Transfer on Death (TOD)
  9 25 deed?
  9 26    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a notary
  9 27 public or other individual authorized to take acknowledgments.
  9 28 Record the form in the public records in the office of the
  9 29 county recorder of each county where the property is located.
  9 30 The form must be acknowledged and recorded before your death or
  9 31 it has no effect.
  9 32    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  9 33    This information may be on the TOD deed. It may also be
  9 34 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  9 35 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
 10  1 consult a lawyer.
 10  2    How do I record the form?
 10  3    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
 10  4 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
 10  5 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
 10  6 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
 10  7 property is located in more than one county, you should record
 10  8 the form in each county.
 10  9    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
 10 10 do?
 10 11    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
 10 12 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
 10 13    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
 10 14    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
 10 15 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
 10 16 lawyer.

 10 16 lawyer.

  9 18    Signature                 Date

  9 20    ACKNOWLEDGMENT
  9 21    (insert acknowledgment here)
  9 22    (back of form)
  9 23    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  9 24    How do I use this form to revoke a Transfer on Death (TOD)
  9 25 deed?
  9 26    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a notary
  9 27 public or other individual authorized to take acknowledgments.
  9 28 Record the form in the public records in the office of the
  9 29 county recorder of each county where the property is located.
  9 30 The form must be acknowledged and recorded before your death or
  9 31 it has no effect.
  9 32    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  9 33    This information may be on the TOD deed. It may also be
  9 34 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  9 35 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
 10  1 consult a lawyer.
 10  2    How do I record the form?
 10  3    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
 10  4 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
 10  5 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
 10  6 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
 10  7 property is located in more than one county, you should record
 10  8 the form in each county.
 10  9    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
 10 10 do?
 10 11    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
 10 12 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
 10 13    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
 10 14    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
 10 15 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
 10 16 lawyer.

 10  4 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
 10  5 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
 10  6 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
 10  7 property is located in more than one county, you should record
 10  8 the form in each county.
 10  9    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
 10 10 do?
 10 11    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
 10 12 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
 10 13    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
 10 14    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
 10 15 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
 10 16 lawyer.

  9 23    COMMON QUESTIONS ABOUT THE USE OF THIS FORM
  9 24    How do I use this form to revoke a Transfer on Death (TOD)
  9 25 deed?
  9 26    Complete this form. Have it acknowledged before a notary
  9 27 public or other individual authorized to take acknowledgments.
  9 28 Record the form in the public records in the office of the
  9 29 county recorder of each county where the property is located.
  9 30 The form must be acknowledged and recorded before your death or
  9 31 it has no effect.
  9 32    How do I find the legal description of the property?
  9 33    This information may be on the TOD deed. It may also be
  9 34 available in the office of the county recorder for the county
  9 35 where the property is located. If you are not absolutely sure,
 10  1 consult a lawyer.

 10  3    Take the completed and acknowledged form to the office
 10  4 of the county recorder of the county where the property is
 10  5 located. Follow the instructions given by the county recorder
 10  6 to make the form part of the official property records. If the
 10  7 property is located in more than one county, you should record
 10  8 the form in each county.
 10  9    I am being pressured to complete this form. What should I
 10 10 do?
 10 11    Do not complete this form under pressure. Seek help from a
 10 12 trusted family member, friend, or lawyer.
 10 13    I have other questions about this form. What should I do?
 10 14    This form is designed to fit some but not all situations.
 10 15 If you have other questions, you are encouraged to consult a
 10 16 lawyer.

 11 21 the subject of the disclaimer is located 11 20 county recorder of the county where the real property that is
 11 21 the subject of the disclaimer is located 11 21 the subject of the disclaimer is located 11 22                           EXPLANATION
 11 23 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
 11 24 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
 11 25    This bill provides that an individual may execute a transfer
 11 26 on death deed which transfers real property outside of probate
 11 27 to one or more beneficiaries effective at the transferor's
 11 28 death.
 11 29    To be valid, a transfer on death deed must contain the
 11 30 essential elements and formalities of a properly recordable
 11 31 inter vivos deed, state that the transfer to the designated
 11 32 beneficiary is to occur at the transferor's death, and be
 11 33 recorded before the transferor's death in the office of the
 11 34 county recorder.
 11 35    A transfer on death deed is revocable, even if the deed
 12  1 states that the deed is irrevocable. A transferor may revoke
 12  2 a transfer on death deed by acknowledging and recording an
 12  3 inconsistent transfer on death deed, or an instrument of
 12  4 revocation or inter vivos deed that expressly revokes the deed.
 12  5    A transfer on death dead is nontestamentary, and the
 12  6 capacity required to make or revoke a transfer on death deed is
 12  7 the same capacity required to make a will.
 12  8    A transfer on death deed is effective even if the beneficiary
 12  9 does not receive notice or delivery of the deed during the
 12 10 transferor's lifetime, and even if the transferor does not
 12 11 receive consideration for the deed.
 12 12    During the transferor's lifetime, a transfer on death deed
 12 13 does not affect the transferor's interest in the property,
 12 14 including the right to transfer or encumber the property, nor
 12 15 does the transfer on death deed create a legal or equitable
 12 16 interest in favor of the designated beneficiary or subject the
 12 17 property to claims of a creditor of the designated beneficiary.
 12 18 If the transferor transfers the property that is the subject
 12 19 of a transfer of death deed before the transferor's death, the
 12 20 transfer on death deed is of no effect at the death of the
 12 21 transferor.
 12 22    At the death of the transferor, subject to Code sections
 12 23 633.238 (elective share of surviving spouse), 633.523 through
 12 24 633.538 (uniform simultaneous death act), and 633.535 through
 12 25 633.537 (felonious death), the property is transferred to the
 12 26 designated beneficiary if the designated beneficiary is alive.
 12 27 If the designated beneficiary predeceases the transferor, the
 12 28 interest of the designated beneficiary lapses.
 12 29    Subject to Code section 558.41 (recording), a beneficiary
 12 30 who takes property under a transfer on death deed takes the
 12 31 property subject to all conveyances, encumbrances, assignments,
 12 32 contracts, mortgages, liens, and other interests to which the
 12 33 property is subject at the transferor's death.
 12 34    If the transferor owns the property as a joint tenant or as
 12 35 a tenant by the entirety, the transfer on death deed is only
 13  1 effective if the transferor is the last surviving joint tenant
 13  2 or tenant by the entirety.
 13  3    A beneficiary may disclaim all or part of the beneficiary's
 13  4 interest as provided by Code chapter 633E (uniform disclaimer
 13  5 of property interest Act).
 13  6    To the extent that the transferor's probate estate is
 13  7 insufficient to satisfy an allowed claim against the estate
 13  8 or a statutory allowance to a surviving spouse or child, the
 13  9 estate may enforce the liability against property transferred
 13 10 at the transferor's death by a transfer on death deed.
 13 11    The bill provides an optional form of a transfer on death
 13 12 deed and an optional form for the revocation of a transfer on
 13 13 death deed.
 13 14    The bill does not affect any deed executed and recorded prior
 13 15 to the effective date of the bill and applies to a transfer on
 13 16 death deed made before, on, or after the effective date of the
 13 17 bill by a transferor dying on or after the effective date of
 13 18 the bill.
 13 19    The bill makes conforming changes.
       LSB 2171XS (4) 87

 12 18 If the transferor transfers the property that is the subject
 12 19 of a transfer of death deed before the transferor's death, the
 12 20 transfer on death deed is of no effect at the death of the
 12 21 transferor.
 12 22    At the death of the transferor, subject to Code sections
 12 23 633.238 (elective share of surviving spouse), 633.523 through
 12 24 633.538 (uniform simultaneous death act), and 633.535 through
 12 25 633.537 (felonious death), the property is transferred to the
 12 26 designated beneficiary if the designated beneficiary is alive.
 12 27 If the designated beneficiary predeceases the transferor, the
 12 28 interest of the designated beneficiary lapses.
 12 29    Subject to Code section 558.41 (recording), a beneficiary
 12 30 who takes property under a transfer on death deed takes the
 12 31 property subject to all conveyances, encumbrances, assignments,
 12 32 contracts, mortgages, liens, and other interests to which the
 12 33 property is subject at the transferor's death.
 12 34    If the transferor owns the property as a joint tenant or as
 12 35 a tenant by the entirety, the transfer on death deed is only
 13  1 effective if the transferor is the last surviving joint tenant
 13  2 or tenant by the entirety.
 13  3    A beneficiary may disclaim all or part of the beneficiary's
 13  4 interest as provided by Code chapter 633E (uniform disclaimer
 13  5 of property interest Act).
 13  6    To the extent that the transferor's probate estate is
 13  7 insufficient to satisfy an allowed claim against the estate
 13  8 or a statutory allowance to a surviving spouse or child, the
 13  9 estate may enforce the liability against property transferred
 13 10 at the transferor's death by a transfer on death deed.
 13 11    The bill provides an optional form of a transfer on death
 13 12 deed and an optional form for the revocation of a transfer on
 13 13 death deed.
 13 14    The bill does not affect any deed executed and recorded prior
 13 15 to the effective date of the bill and applies to a transfer on
 13 16 death deed made before, on, or after the effective date of the
 13 17 bill by a transferor dying on or after the effective date of
 13 18 the bill.
 13 19    The bill makes conforming changes.
       LSB 2171XS (4) 87
       jh/rj
 11 25    This bill provides that an individual may execute a transfer
 11 26 on death deed which transfers real property outside of probate
 11 27 to one or more beneficiaries effective at the transferor's
 11 28 death.
 11 29    To be valid, a transfer on death deed must contain the
 11 30 essential elements and formalities of a properly recordable
 11 31 inter vivos deed, state that the transfer to the designated
 11 32 beneficiary is to occur at the transferor's death, and be
 11 33 recorded before the transferor's death in the office of the
 11 34 county recorder.
 11 35    A transfer on death deed is revocable, even if the deed
 12  1 states that the deed is irrevocable. A transferor may revoke
 12  2 a transfer on death deed by acknowledging and recording an
 12  3 inconsistent transfer on death deed, or an instrument of
 12  4 revocation or inter vivos deed that expressly revokes the deed.
 12  5    A transfer on death dead is nontestamentary, and the
 12  6 capacity required to make or revoke a transfer on death deed is
 12  7 the same capacity required to make a will.
 12  8    A transfer on death deed is effective even if the beneficiary
 12  9 does not receive notice or delivery of the deed during the
 12 10 transferor's lifetime, and even if the transferor does not
 12 11 receive consideration for the deed.
 12 12    During the transferor's lifetime, a transfer on death deed
 12 13 does not affect the transferor's interest in the property,
 12 14 including the right to transfer or encumber the property, nor
 12 15 does the transfer on death deed create a legal or equitable
 12 16 interest in favor of the designated beneficiary or subject the
 12 17 property to claims of a creditor of the designated beneficiary.
 12 18 If the transferor transfers the property that is the subject
 12 19 of a transfer of death deed before the transferor's death, the
 12 20 transfer on death deed is of no effect at the death of the
 12 21 transferor.
 12 22    At the death of the transferor, subject to Code sections
 12 23 633.238 (elective share of surviving spouse), 633.523 through
 12 24 633.538 (uniform simultaneous death act), and 633.535 through
 12 25 633.537 (felonious death), the property is transferred to the
 12 26 designated beneficiary if the designated beneficiary is alive.
 12 27 If the designated beneficiary predeceases the transferor, the
 12 28 interest of the designated beneficiary lapses.
 12 29    Subject to Code section 558.41 (recording), a beneficiary
 12 30 who takes property under a transfer on death deed takes the
 12 31 property subject to all conveyances, encumbrances, assignments,
 12 32 contracts, mortgages, liens, and other interests to which the
 12 33 property is subject at the transferor's death.
 12 34    If the transferor owns the property as a joint tenant or as
 12 35 a tenant by the entirety, the transfer on death deed is only
 13  1 effective if the transferor is the last surviving joint tenant
 13  2 or tenant by the entirety.
 13  3    A beneficiary may disclaim all or part of the beneficiary's
 13  4 interest as provided by Code chapter 633E (uniform disclaimer
 13  5 of property interest Act).
 13  6    To the extent that the transferor's probate estate is
 13  7 insufficient to satisfy an allowed claim against the estate
 13  8 or a statutory allowance to a surviving spouse or child, the
 13  9 estate may enforce the liability against property transferred
 13 10 at the transferor's death by a transfer on death deed.
 13 11    The bill provides an optional form of a transfer on death
 13 12 deed and an optional form for the revocation of a transfer on
 13 13 death deed.
 13 14    The bill does not affect any deed executed and recorded prior
 13 15 to the effective date of the bill and applies to a transfer on
 13 16 death deed made before, on, or after the effective date of the
 13 17 bill by a transferor dying on or after the effective date of
 13 18 the bill.
 13 19    The bill makes conforming changes.
