 13 13 death deed.
 13 14    The bill does not affect any deed executed and recorded prior
 13 15 to the effective date of the bill and applies to a transfer on
 13 16 death deed made before, on, or after the effective date of the
 13 17 bill by a transferor dying on or after the effective date of
 13 18 the bill.
 13 19    The bill makes conforming changes.
       LSB 2171XS (4) 87
       jh/rj
 11 33 recorded before the transferor's death in the office of the
 11 34 county recorder.
 11 35    A transfer on death deed is revocable, even if the deed
 12  1 states that the deed is irrevocable. A transferor may revoke
 12  2 a transfer on death deed by acknowledging and recording an
 12  3 inconsistent transfer on death deed, or an instrument of
 12  4 revocation or inter vivos deed that expressly revokes the deed.
 12  5    A transfer on death dead is nontestamentary, and the
 12  6 capacity required to make or revoke a transfer on death deed is
 12  7 the same capacity required to make a will.
 12  8    A transfer on death deed is effective even if the beneficiary
 12  9 does not receive notice or delivery of the deed during the
 12 10 transferor's lifetime, and even if the transferor does not
 12 11 receive consideration for the deed.
 12 12    During the transferor's lifetime, a transfer on death deed
 12 13 does not affect the transferor's interest in the property,
 12 14 including the right to transfer or encumber the property, nor
 12 15 does the transfer on death deed create a legal or equitable
 12 16 interest in favor of the designated beneficiary or subject the
 12 17 property to claims of a creditor of the designated beneficiary.
 12 18 If the transferor transfers the property that is the subject
 12 19 of a transfer of death deed before the transferor's death, the
 12 20 transfer on death deed is of no effect at the death of the
 12 21 transferor.
 12 22    At the death of the transferor, subject to Code sections
 12 23 633.238 (elective share of surviving spouse), 633.523 through
 12 24 633.538 (uniform simultaneous death act), and 633.535 through
 12 25 633.537 (felonious death), the property is transferred to the
 12 26 designated beneficiary if the designated beneficiary is alive.
 12 27 If the designated beneficiary predeceases the transferor, the
 12 28 interest of the designated beneficiary lapses.
 12 29    Subject to Code section 558.41 (recording), a beneficiary
 12 30 who takes property under a transfer on death deed takes the
 12 31 property subject to all conveyances, encumbrances, assignments,
 12 32 contracts, mortgages, liens, and other interests to which the
 12 33 property is subject at the transferor's death.
 12 34    If the transferor owns the property as a joint tenant or as
 12 35 a tenant by the entirety, the transfer on death deed is only
 13  1 effective if the transferor is the last surviving joint tenant
 13  2 or tenant by the entirety.
 13  3    A beneficiary may disclaim all or part of the beneficiary's
 13  4 interest as provided by Code chapter 633E (uniform disclaimer
 13  5 of property interest Act).
 13  6    To the extent that the transferor's probate estate is
 13  7 insufficient to satisfy an allowed claim against the estate
 13  8 or a statutory allowance to a surviving spouse or child, the
 13  9 estate may enforce the liability against property transferred
 13 10 at the transferor's death by a transfer on death deed.
 13 11    The bill provides an optional form of a transfer on death
 13 12 deed and an optional form for the revocation of a transfer on
 13 13 death deed.
 13 14    The bill does not affect any deed executed and recorded prior
 13 15 to the effective date of the bill and applies to a transfer on
 13 16 death deed made before, on, or after the effective date of the
 13 17 bill by a transferor dying on or after the effective date of
 13 18 the bill.
 13 19    The bill makes conforming changes.

 13  5 of property interest Act).
 13  6    To the extent that the transferor's probate estate is
 13  7 insufficient to satisfy an allowed claim against the estate
 13  8 or a statutory allowance to a surviving spouse or child, the
 13  9 estate may enforce the liability against property transferred
 13 10 at the transferor's death by a transfer on death deed.
 13 11    The bill provides an optional form of a transfer on death
 13 12 deed and an optional form for the revocation of a transfer on
 13 13 death deed.
 13 14    The bill does not affect any deed executed and recorded prior
 13 15 to the effective date of the bill and applies to a transfer on
 13 16 death deed made before, on, or after the effective date of the
 13 17 bill by a transferor dying on or after the effective date of
 13 18 the bill.
 13 19    The bill makes conforming changes.
       LSB 2171XS (4) 87
       jh/rj
 12  8    A transfer on death deed is effective even if the beneficiary
 12  9 does not receive notice or delivery of the deed during the
 12 10 transferor's lifetime, and even if the transferor does not
 12 11 receive consideration for the deed.
 12 12    During the transferor's lifetime, a transfer on death deed
 12 13 does not affect the transferor's interest in the property,
 12 14 including the right to transfer or encumber the property, nor
 12 15 does the transfer on death deed create a legal or equitable
 12 16 interest in favor of the designated beneficiary or subject the
 12 17 property to claims of a creditor of the designated beneficiary.
 12 18 If the transferor transfers the property that is the subject
 12 19 of a transfer of death deed before the transferor's death, the
 12 20 transfer on death deed is of no effect at the death of the
 12 21 transferor.
 12 22    At the death of the transferor, subject to Code sections
 12 23 633.238 (elective share of surviving spouse), 633.523 through
 12 24 633.538 (uniform simultaneous death act), and 633.535 through
 12 25 633.537 (felonious death), the property is transferred to the
 12 26 designated beneficiary if the designated beneficiary is alive.
 12 27 If the designated beneficiary predeceases the transferor, the
 12 28 interest of the designated beneficiary lapses.
 12 29    Subject to Code section 558.41 (recording), a beneficiary
 12 30 who takes property under a transfer on death deed takes the
 12 31 property subject to all conveyances, encumbrances, assignments,
 12 32 contracts, mortgages, liens, and other interests to which the
 12 33 property is subject at the transferor's death.
 12 34    If the transferor owns the property as a joint tenant or as
 12 35 a tenant by the entirety, the transfer on death deed is only
 13  1 effective if the transferor is the last surviving joint tenant
 13  2 or tenant by the entirety.
 13  3    A beneficiary may disclaim all or part of the beneficiary's
 13  4 interest as provided by Code chapter 633E (uniform disclaimer
 13  5 of property interest Act).

 12 27 If the designated beneficiary predeceases the transferor, the
 12 28 interest of the designated beneficiary lapses.
 12 29    Subject to Code section 558.41 (recording), a beneficiary
 12 30 who takes property under a transfer on death deed takes the
 12 31 property subject to all conveyances, encumbrances, assignments,
 12 32 contracts, mortgages, liens, and other interests to which the
 12 33 property is subject at the transferor's death.
 12 34    If the transferor owns the property as a joint tenant or as
 12 35 a tenant by the entirety, the transfer on death deed is only
 13  1 effective if the transferor is the last surviving joint tenant
 13  2 or tenant by the entirety.
 13  3    A beneficiary may disclaim all or part of the beneficiary's
 13  4 interest as provided by Code chapter 633E (uniform disclaimer
 13  5 of property interest Act).
 13  6    To the extent that the transferor's probate estate is
 13  7 insufficient to satisfy an allowed claim against the estate
 13  8 or a statutory allowance to a surviving spouse or child, the
 13  9 estate may enforce the liability against property transferred
 13 10 at the transferor's death by a transfer on death deed.
 13 11    The bill provides an optional form of a transfer on death
 13 12 deed and an optional form for the revocation of a transfer on
 13 13 death deed.
 13 14    The bill does not affect any deed executed and recorded prior
 13 15 to the effective date of the bill and applies to a transfer on
 13 16 death deed made before, on, or after the effective date of the
 13 17 bill by a transferor dying on or after the effective date of
 13 18 the bill.
 13 19    The bill makes conforming changes.
       LSB 2171XS (4) 87
       jh/rj

 13  7 insufficient to satisfy an allowed claim against the estate
 13  8 or a statutory allowance to a surviving spouse or child, the
 13  9 estate may enforce the liability against property transferred
 13 10 at the transferor's death by a transfer on death deed.
 13 11    The bill provides an optional form of a transfer on death
 13 12 deed and an optional form for the revocation of a transfer on
 13 13 death deed.
 13 14    The bill does not affect any deed executed and recorded prior
 13 15 to the effective date of the bill and applies to a transfer on
 13 16 death deed made before, on, or after the effective date of the
 13 17 bill by a transferor dying on or after the effective date of
 13 18 the bill.
 13 19    The bill makes conforming changes.
